</tbody></table>
</div>
</div>
<p>The country's most prevalent religion is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theravada_Buddhism" title="Theravada Buddhism">Theravada Buddhism</a>, which is an integral part of Thai identity and culture. Active participation in Buddhism is among the highest in the world. Thailand has the second-largest number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhists</a> in the world after China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PewDec2012_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-PewDec2012-207">[196]</a></sup> According to the 2000 census, 94.6% and 93.58% in 2010 of the country's population self-identified as Buddhists of the Theravada tradition.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phutthamonthon_Buddha.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Phutthamonthon_Buddha.JPG/220px-Phutthamonthon_Buddha.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Phutthamonthon_Buddha.JPG/330px-Phutthamonthon_Buddha.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Phutthamonthon_Buddha.JPG/440px-Phutthamonthon_Buddha.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phutthamonthon_Buddha.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Samanera" title="Samanera">Samanera</a></i> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theravada_Buddhism" title="Theravada Buddhism">Theravada Buddhism</a>, the most practised religion in Thailand.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Thailand" title="Islam in Thailand">Muslims</a> constitute the second largest religious group in Thailand, comprising 5.4% of the population in 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Department_of_State,_Thailand_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_Department_of_State,_Thailand-208">[197]</a></sup> Islam is concentrated mostly in the country's southernmost provinces: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pattani" title="Pattani">Pattani</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yala_Province" title="Yala Province">Yala</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satun_Province" title="Satun Province">Satun</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narathiwat_Province" title="Narathiwat Province">Narathiwat</a>, and part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Songkhla_Province" title="Songkhla Province">Songkhla</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chumphon_Province" title="Chumphon Province">Chumphon</a>, which are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Malays_(ethnic_group)" title="Malays (ethnic group)">Malay</a>, most of whom are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslims</a>. Christians represented 1.13% (2018) of the population in 2018, with the remaining population consisting of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Thailand#Thailand" title="Hinduism in Thailand">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism_in_Thailand" title="Sikhism in Thailand">Sikhs</a>, who live mostly in the country's cities. There is also a small but historically significant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jews_and_Judaism_in_Thailand" title="Jews and Judaism in Thailand">Jewish community in Thailand</a> dating back to the 17th century.
</p><p>The constitution does not name official state religion, and provides for freedom of religion. Even the authority formally does not register new religious groups that have not been accepted and limit the number of missionaries, unregistered religious organisations as well as missionaries who are allowed to operate freely. There have been no widespread reports of societal abuses or discrimination based on religious belief or practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[198]</a></sup> Thai law officially recognizes five religious groups: Buddhists, Muslims, Brahmin-Hindus, Sikhs, and Christians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[199]</a></sup> However, some laws are inspired from Buddhist practices, such as banning alcohol sales on religious holidays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[200]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Thailand" title="Education in Thailand">Education in Thailand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chulalongkorn_University_Auditorium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Chulalongkorn_University_Auditorium.jpg/220px-Chulalongkorn_University_Auditorium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Chulalongkorn_University_Auditorium.jpg/330px-Chulalongkorn_University_Auditorium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Chulalongkorn_University_Auditorium.jpg/440px-Chulalongkorn_University_Auditorium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chulalongkorn_University_Auditorium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chulalongkorn_University" title="Chulalongkorn University">Chulalongkorn University</a>, established in 1917, is the oldest university in Thailand.</div></div></div>
<p>Thailand's youth literacy rate was 98.1% in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[201]</a></sup> Education is provided by a well-organised school system of kindergartens, primary, lower secondary and upper secondary schools, numerous vocational colleges, and universities. Education is compulsory up to and including age 14, with the government is mandated to provide free education through to age 17. The establishment of reliable and coherent curricula for its primary and secondary schools is subject to rapid changes. Issues concerning university entrance has been in constant upheaval for a number of years. The country is also one of the few that still mandates uniform up to the university years, which is still a subject of ongoing debate. The quality of providing education in the country is often questioned.
</p><p>In 2013, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Information and Communication Technology (Thailand)">Ministry of Information and Communication Technology</a> announced that 27,231 schools would receive classroom-level access to <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">high-speed internet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[202]</a></sup> However, the country's educational infrastructure was still underprepared for online teaching, as smaller and more remote schools were particularly hindered by COVID-19 restrictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[203]</a></sup>
</p><p>The number of higher education institutions in Thailand has grown strongly over the past decades to 156 officially. The two top-ranking universities in Thailand are <a href="/wiki/Chulalongkorn_University" title="Chulalongkorn University">Chulalongkorn University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahidol_University" title="Mahidol University">Mahidol University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[204]</a></sup> Thai universities research output still relatively low, even though the country's journal publications increased by 20% between 2011 and 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[205]</a></sup> Recent initiatives, such as the <i>National Research University</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[206]</a></sup> and <i>Graduate research intensive university: VISTEC</i>, are designed to strengthen Thailand's national research universities.
</p><p>The private sector of education is well developed and significantly contributes to the overall provision of education. Thailand has the second highest number of English-medium private international schools in <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">Southeast Asian Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Education_in_Thailand_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-Education_in_Thailand-218">[207]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cram_school" title="Cram school">Cram schools</a> are especially popular for university entrance exams.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png/220px-%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png/330px-%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png/440px-%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thailand is a country where <a href="/wiki/School_uniforms_in_Thailand" title="School uniforms in Thailand">school uniform is mandatory</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Students in ethnic minority areas score consistently lower in standardised national and international tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DraperJ2012_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-DraperJ2012-219">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECDTH2013_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECDTH2013-220">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[210]</a></sup>
This is likely due to unequal allocation of educational resources, weak teacher training, poverty, and low Thai language skill, the language of the tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DraperJ2012_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-DraperJ2012-219">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[212]</a></sup> As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Thailand&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Thailand was ranked 89th out of 100 countries globally for English proficiency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>Extensive nationwide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IQ" title="IQ">IQ</a> tests were administered to 72,780 Thai students from December 2010 to January 2011. The average IQ was found to be 98.59, which is higher than previous studies have found. IQ levels were found to be inconsistent throughout the country, with the lowest average of 88.07 found in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narathiwat_Province" title="Narathiwat Province">Narathiwat Province</a> and the highest average of 108.91 reported in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nonthaburi_Province" title="Nonthaburi Province">Nonthaburi Province</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Health_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Public Health (Thailand)">Ministry of Public Health</a> blamed the discrepancies on <a href="/wiki/Iodine_deficiency" title="Iodine deficiency">iodine deficiency</a>, and required that <a href="/wiki/Iodised_salt" title="Iodised salt">iodine be added to table salt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[214]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thailand is the third most popular study destination in ASEAN. The number of international degree students in Thailand increased by 9.7 times between 1999 and 2012, from 1,882 to 20,309 students. Most of international students come from neighbor countries<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Education_in_Thailand_218-1"><a href="#cite_note-Education_in_Thailand-218">[207]</a></sup> from China, Myanmar, Cambodia and Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[215]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Thailand" title="Health in Thailand">Health in Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Thailand" title="Healthcare in Thailand">Healthcare in Thailand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hospitals_in_Thailand" title="Hospitals in Thailand">Hospitals in Thailand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siriraj_Hospital,Bangkok.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2394" data-file-width="4256" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Siriraj_Hospital%2CBangkok.jpg/220px-Siriraj_Hospital%2CBangkok.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Siriraj_Hospital%2CBangkok.jpg/330px-Siriraj_Hospital%2CBangkok.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Siriraj_Hospital%2CBangkok.jpg/440px-Siriraj_Hospital%2CBangkok.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siriraj_Hospital,Bangkok.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Siriraj_Hospital" title="Siriraj Hospital">Siriraj Hospital</a> in Bangkok, the oldest and largest hospital in Thailand.</div></div></div>
<p>Thailand ranks world's sixth, and Asia's first in the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Global_Health_Security_Index" title="Global Health Security Index">Global Health Security Index</a> of global health security capabilities in 195 countries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[216]</a></sup> making it the only <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a> on the world's top ten. Thailand had 62 hospitals accredited by <a href="/wiki/Joint_Commission" title="Joint Commission">Joint Commission</a> International.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[217]</a></sup> In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Bumrungrad_International_Hospital" title="Bumrungrad International Hospital">Bumrungrad</a> became the first hospital in Asia to meet the standard.
</p><p>Health and medical care is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Health_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Public Health (Thailand)">Ministry of Public Health</a> (MOPH), along with several other non-ministerial government agencies, with total national expenditures on health amounting to 4.3 percent of GDP in 2009. <a href="/wiki/Non-communicable_disease" title="Non-communicable disease">Non-communicable diseases</a> form the major burden of morbidity and mortality, while infectious diseases including malaria and tuberculosis, as well as traffic accidents, are also important public health issues. The current Minister for Public Health is <a href="/wiki/Anutin_Charnvirakul" title="Anutin Charnvirakul">Anutin Charnvirakul</a>.
</p><p>In December 2018 the interim parliament voted to legalise the use of <a href="/wiki/Cannabis" title="Cannabis">cannabis</a> for medical reasons, making Thailand the first Southeast Asian country to allow the use of <a href="/wiki/Medical_cannabis" title="Medical cannabis">medical cannabis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[218]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Thailand" title="Culture of Thailand">Culture of Thailand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4800" data-file-width="3200" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/140px-Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/210px-Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/280px-Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thai women wearing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sabai" title="Sabai">sabai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thompson_House" title="Jim Thompson House">Jim Thompson House</a></div></div></div>
<p>Thai culture and traditions incorporate a great deal of influence from India, China, Cambodia, and the rest of Southeast Asia. Thailand's national religion, Theravada Buddhism, is central to modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_identity" title="Thai identity">Thai identity</a>. <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Thailand" title="Buddhism in Thailand">Thai Buddhism</a> has evolved over time to include many regional beliefs originating from <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>, as well as ancestor worship. The <a href="/wiki/Thai_solar_calendar" title="Thai solar calendar">official calendar</a> in Thailand is based on the Eastern version of the <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_calendar" title="Buddhist calendar">Buddhist Era</a> (BE). Thai identity today is a <a href="/wiki/Thaification" title="Thaification">social construct</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phibun" title="Phibun">Phibun</a> regime in 1940s.
</p><p>Several ethnic groups mediated change between their traditional local culture, national Thai, and global cultural influences. <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Overseas Chinese</a> also form a significant part of Thai society, particularly in and around Bangkok. Their successful integration into Thai society has allowed them to hold positions of economic and political power. Thai Chinese businesses prosper as part of the larger <a href="/wiki/Bamboo_network" title="Bamboo network">bamboo network</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weidenbaum_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weidenbaum-230">[219]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loi_Krathong_2010_John_Shedrick.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="849" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Loi_Krathong_2010_John_Shedrick.jpg/220px-Loi_Krathong_2010_John_Shedrick.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Loi_Krathong_2010_John_Shedrick.jpg/330px-Loi_Krathong_2010_John_Shedrick.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Loi_Krathong_2010_John_Shedrick.jpg/440px-Loi_Krathong_2010_John_Shedrick.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Loi_Krathong_2010_John_Shedrick.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People floating krathong rafts during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loi_Krathong" title="Loi Krathong">Loi Krathong</a> festival in Chiang Mai, Thailand</div></div></div>
<p>Respects for elderly and superiors (by age, position, monks, or certain professions) is Thai <a href="/wiki/Mores" title="Mores">mores</a>. As with other Asian cultures, respect towards ancestors is an essential part of Thai spiritual practice. Thais have strong sense of social hierarchy, reflecting in many classes of <a href="/wiki/Thai_honorifics" title="Thai honorifics">honorifics</a>. Elders have by tradition ruled in family decisions or ceremonies. <i><a href="/wiki/Thai_greeting" title="Thai greeting">Wai</a></i> is a traditional Thai greeting, and is generally offered first by person who is younger or lower in social status and position. Older siblings have duties to younger ones. Thais have a strong sense of hospitality and generosity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Taboos in Thai culture include touching someone's head or pointing with the feet, as the head is considered the most sacred and the foot the lowest part of the body.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Thai_art" title="Thai art">Thai art</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WatPhraKeaw_Ramayana_Chariot.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/WatPhraKeaw_Ramayana_Chariot.JPG/220px-WatPhraKeaw_Ramayana_Chariot.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/WatPhraKeaw_Ramayana_Chariot.JPG/330px-WatPhraKeaw_Ramayana_Chariot.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/WatPhraKeaw_Ramayana_Chariot.JPG/440px-WatPhraKeaw_Ramayana_Chariot.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WatPhraKeaw_Ramayana_Chariot.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scene from the <a href="/wiki/Ramakien" title="Ramakien">Ramakien</a> depicted on a mural at <a href="/wiki/Wat_Phra_Kaew" title="Wat Phra Kaew">Wat Phra Kaew</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The origins of Thai art were very much influenced by <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_art" title="Buddhist art">Buddhist art</a> and by scenes from the Indian epics. Traditional Thai <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculpture</a> almost exclusively depicts <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddha_image" title="Buddha image">images of the Buddha</a>, being very similar with the other styles from <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. Traditional Thai <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">paintings</a> usually consist of book illustrations, and painted ornamentation of buildings such as <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">palaces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Temple" title="Temple">temples</a>. Thai art was influenced by indigenous civilisations of the <a href="/wiki/Dvaravati" title="Dvaravati">Mon</a> and other civilisations. By the Sukothai and Ayutthaya period, thai had developed into its own unique style and was later further influenced by the other Asian styles, mostly by <a href="/wiki/Indian_art" title="Indian art">Sri Lankan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_art" title="Chinese art">Chinese</a>. Thai sculpture and painting, and the royal courts provided patronage, erecting temples and other religious shrines as acts of merit or to commemorate important events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-231">[220]</a></sup>
</p><p>Traditional Thai paintings showed subjects in two <a href="/wiki/Dimension" title="Dimension">dimensions</a> without <a href="/wiki/Perspective_(graphical)" title="Perspective (graphical)">perspective</a>. The size of each element in the picture reflected its degree of importance. The primary technique of <a href="/wiki/Composition_(visual_arts)" title="Composition (visual arts)">composition</a> is that of apportioning areas: the main elements are isolated from each other by space transformers. This eliminated the intermediate ground, which would otherwise imply perspective. Perspective was introduced only as a result of <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> influence in the mid-19th century. Monk artist <a href="/wiki/Khrua_In_Khong" title="Khrua In Khong">Khrua In Khong</a> is well known as the first artist to introduce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_perspective" title="Linear perspective">linear perspective</a> to Thai traditional art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[221]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most frequent narrative subjects for paintings were or are: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jataka" title="Jataka">Jataka</a> stories, episodes from the life of the <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">Buddha</a>, the Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Heaven" title="Heaven">heavens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hell" title="Hell">hells</a>, themes derived from the Thai versions of the Ramayana and Mahabharata, not to mention scenes of daily life. Some of the scenes are influenced by <a href="/wiki/Thai_folklore" title="Thai folklore">Thai folklore</a> instead of following strict Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Iconography" title="Iconography">iconography</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-231">[220]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Thailand" title="Architecture of Thailand">Architecture of Thailand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_sculptures_of_two_mythical_giant_demons,_Thotsakan_and_Sahatsadecha,_guarding_the_eastern_gate_of_the_main_chapel_of_Wat_Arun,_Bangkok.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="7360" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/The_sculptures_of_two_mythical_giant_demons%2C_Thotsakan_and_Sahatsadecha%2C_guarding_the_eastern_gate_of_the_main_chapel_of_Wat_Arun%2C_Bangkok.jpg/220px-The_sculptures_of_two_mythical_giant_demons%2C_Thotsakan_and_Sahatsadecha%2C_guarding_the_eastern_gate_of_the_main_chapel_of_Wat_Arun%2C_Bangkok.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/The_sculptures_of_two_mythical_giant_demons%2C_Thotsakan_and_Sahatsadecha%2C_guarding_the_eastern_gate_of_the_main_chapel_of_Wat_Arun%2C_Bangkok.jpg/330px-The_sculptures_of_two_mythical_giant_demons%2C_Thotsakan_and_Sahatsadecha%2C_guarding_the_eastern_gate_of_the_main_chapel_of_Wat_Arun%2C_Bangkok.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/The_sculptures_of_two_mythical_giant_demons%2C_Thotsakan_and_Sahatsadecha%2C_guarding_the_eastern_gate_of_the_main_chapel_of_Wat_Arun%2C_Bangkok.jpg/440px-The_sculptures_of_two_mythical_giant_demons%2C_Thotsakan_and_Sahatsadecha%2C_guarding_the_eastern_gate_of_the_main_chapel_of_Wat_Arun%2C_Bangkok.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_sculptures_of_two_mythical_giant_demons,_Thotsakan_and_Sahatsadecha,_guarding_the_eastern_gate_of_the_main_chapel_of_Wat_Arun,_Bangkok.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two sculptures guarding the eastern gate to the main chapel of <a href="/wiki/Wat_Arun" title="Wat Arun">Wat Arun</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Architecture is the preeminent medium of the country's cultural legacy and reflects both the challenges of living in Thailand's sometimes extreme climate as well as, historically, the importance of architecture to the Thai people's sense of community and religious beliefs. Influenced by the architectural traditions of many of Thailand's neighbours, it has also developed significant regional variation within its vernacular and religious buildings.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya Kingdom</a> movement, which went from approximately 1350 to 1767, was one of the most fruitful and creative periods in Thai architecture The identity of architecture in Ayutthaya period is designed to display might and riches so it has great size and appearance. The temples in Ayutthaya seldom built eaves stretching from the masterhead. The dominant feature of this style is sunlight shining into buildings. During the latter part of the Ayutthaya period, architecture was regarded as a peak achievement that responded to the requirements of people and expressed the gracefulness of Thainess.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[222]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist_temples_in_Thailand" title="Buddhist temples in Thailand">Buddhist temples in Thailand</a> are known as "<a href="/wiki/Wat" title="Wat">wats</a>", from the <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pāḷi</a> <i>vāṭa</i>, meaning an enclosure. A temple has an enclosing wall that divides it from the secular world. Wat <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a> has seen many changes in Thailand in the course of history. Although there are many differences in layout and style, they all adhere to the same principles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Thai_literature" title="Thai literature">Thai literature</a></div>
<p>Thai literature has had a long history. Even before the establishment of the Sukhothai Kingdom there existed oral and written works.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Sukhothai_Kingdom" title="Sukhothai Kingdom">Sukhothai Kingdom</a>, Most literary works were written in simple prose with certain alliteration schemes. Major works include King <a href="/wiki/Ram_Khamhaeng_Inscription" title="Ram Khamhaeng Inscription">Ram Khamhaeng Inscription</a> describing life at the time, which is considered the first literary work in Thai script, but some historians questioned its authenticity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Terwiel_2007_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-Terwiel_2007-235">[224]</a></sup> <i>Trai Phum <a href="/wiki/Phra_Ruang" title="Phra Ruang">Phra Ruang</a></i>, written in 1345 by King <a href="/wiki/Maha_Thammaracha_I" title="Maha Thammaracha I">Maha Thammaracha I</a>, expounds Buddhist philosophy based on a profound and extensive study with reference to over 30 sacred texts and could be considered the nation's first piece of research <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dissertation" title="Dissertation">dissertation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[225]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunrise_on_Hat_Saikaew,_Koh_Samet.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Sunrise_on_Hat_Saikaew%2C_Koh_Samet.jpg/220px-Sunrise_on_Hat_Saikaew%2C_Koh_Samet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Sunrise_on_Hat_Saikaew%2C_Koh_Samet.jpg/330px-Sunrise_on_Hat_Saikaew%2C_Koh_Samet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Sunrise_on_Hat_Saikaew%2C_Koh_Samet.jpg/440px-Sunrise_on_Hat_Saikaew%2C_Koh_Samet.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sunrise_on_Hat_Saikaew,_Koh_Samet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sculptures of <a href="/wiki/Phra_Aphai_Mani" title="Phra Aphai Mani">Phra Aphai Mani</a> and the Mermaid from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epic_poem" title="Epic poem">epic poem</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Phra_Aphai_Mani" title="Phra Aphai Mani">Phra Aphai Mani</a></i>, a work of <a href="/wiki/Sunthorn_Phu" title="Sunthorn Phu">Sunthorn Phu</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya Kingdom</a>, new <a href="/wiki/Thai_poetry" title="Thai poetry">poetic</a> forms were created, with different rhyme schemes and metres. It is common to find a combination of different poetic forms in one poetic work. <i>Lilit <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Phai" title="Yuan Phai">Yuan Phai</a></i> is a narrative poem describing <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya%E2%80%93Lan_Na_War_(1441%E2%80%931474)" title="Ayutthaya–Lan Na War (1441–1474)">the war</a> between King <a href="/wiki/Borommatrailokkanat" title="Borommatrailokkanat">Borommatrailokkanat</a> of Ayutthaya and Prince <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tilokkarat" title="Tilokkarat">Tilokkarat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lan_Na" title="Lan Na">Lan Na</a>. One of the most beautiful literary works is <i>Kap He Ruea</i> composed by Prince <a href="/wiki/Thammathibet" title="Thammathibet">Thammathibet</a> in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nirat" title="Nirat">nirat</a></i> tradition. Traditionally, the verse is sung during the colourful royal barge procession and has been the model for subsequent poets to emulate. The same prince also composed the greatly admired <i>Kap Ho Khlong</i> on the Visit to Than Thongdaeng and <i>Kap Ho Khlong Nirat Phrabat</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thaiembassy_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-thaiembassy-237">[226]</a></sup> Despite its short period of 15 years, <a href="/wiki/Thonburi_Kingdom" title="Thonburi Kingdom">Thon Buri</a> Period produced <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramakian" title="Ramakian">Ramakian</a></i>, a verse drama contributed by King <a href="/wiki/Taksin" title="Taksin">Taksin</a> the Great. The era marked the revival of literature after the fall of Ayutthaya.
</p><p>During the 18th century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rattanakosin_Kingdom" title="Rattanakosin Kingdom">Rattanakosin</a> period, which still fought with the Burmese, many of the early Rattanakosin works deal with war and military strategy. Some examples are <i>Nirat Rop Phama Thi Tha Din Daeng</i>, <i>Phleng Yao Rop Phama Thi Nakhon Si Thammarat</i>. In the performing arts, perhaps the most important dramatic achievement is the complete work of <i>Ramakian</i> by King <a href="/wiki/Rama_I" title="Rama I">Rama I</a>. In addition, There were also verse recitals with musical accompaniment, such as <a href="/wiki/Mahori" title="Mahori">Mahori</a> telling the story of <i><a href="/wiki/Kaki_Klon_Suphap" title="Kaki Klon Suphap">Kaki</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Sepha" title="Sepha">Sepha</a> relating the story of <i><a href="/wiki/Khun_Chang_Khun_Phaen" title="Khun Chang Khun Phaen">Khun Chang Khun Phaen</a></i>. Other recitals include <a href="/wiki/Sri_Thanonchai" title="Sri Thanonchai">Sri Thanonchai</a>. The most important Thai poet in this period was <a href="/wiki/Sunthorn_Phu" title="Sunthorn Phu">Sunthorn Phu</a> (สุนทรภู่) (1786–1855), widely known as "the bard of Rattanakosin" (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">กวีเอกแห่งกรุงรัตนโกสินทร์</span>). Sunthorn Phu is best known for his epic poem <i><a href="/wiki/Phra_Aphai_Mani" title="Phra Aphai Mani">Phra Aphai Mani</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">พระอภัยมณี</span>), written during 1822 and 1844. <i>Phra Aphai Mani</i> is a versified fantasy-adventure novel, a genre of Siamese literature known as <span title="Thai-language romanization"><i lang="th-Latn">nithan kham klon</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">นิทานคำกลอน</span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thaiembassy_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-thaiembassy-237">[226]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some of the most well-known modern Thai writers include <a href="/wiki/Kukrit_Pramoj" title="Kukrit Pramoj">Kukrit Pramoj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kulap_Saipradit" title="Kulap Saipradit">Kulap Saipradit</a>, (penname <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siburapha" title="Siburapha">Siburapha</a>), Suweeriya Sirisingh (penname Botan), <a href="/wiki/Chart_Korbjitti" title="Chart Korbjitti">Chart Korbjitti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prabda_Yoon" title="Prabda Yoon">Prabda Yoon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duanwad_Pimwana" title="Duanwad Pimwana">Duanwad Pimwana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[227]</a></sup> The works tended to be light fiction.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Thailand" title="Music of Thailand">Music of Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Thailand" title="Dance in Thailand">Dance in Thailand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dance_of_the_Ramayana.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Dance_of_the_Ramayana.jpg/220px-Dance_of_the_Ramayana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Dance_of_the_Ramayana.jpg/330px-Dance_of_the_Ramayana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Dance_of_the_Ramayana.jpg/440px-Dance_of_the_Ramayana.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dance_of_the_Ramayana.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Khon" title="Khon">Khon</a> show is the most stylised form of Thai performance.</div></div></div>
<p>Aside from folk and regional dances (southern Thailand's <a href="/wiki/Menora_(dance)" title="Menora (dance)">Menora (dance)</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramwong" title="Ramwong">Ramwong</a>, for example), the two major forms of Thai classical dance drama are <a href="/wiki/Khon" title="Khon">Khon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lakhon_nai" title="Lakhon nai">Lakhon nai</a>. In the beginning, both were exclusively court entertainments and it was not until much later that a popular style of dance theatre, <a href="/wiki/Likay" title="Likay">likay</a>, evolved as a diversion for common folk who had no access to royal performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>Folk dance forms include dance theater forms like <a href="/wiki/Likay" title="Likay">likay</a>, numerous regional dances (<i>ram</i>), the ritual dance <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ram_muay" title="Ram muay">ram muay</a>, and homage to the teacher, <a href="/wiki/Wai_khru_ram_muay" title="Wai khru ram muay">wai khru</a>. Both ram muay and wai khru take place before all traditional <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">muay Thai</a> matches. The wai is also an annual ceremony performed by Thai classical dance groups to honor their artistic ancestors.
</p><p>Thai classical music is synonymous with those stylized court ensembles and repertoires that emerged in their present form within the royal centers of Central Thailand some 800 years ago. These ensembles, while being influenced by older practices are today uniquely Thai expressions. While the three primary classical ensembles, the <a href="/wiki/Piphat" title="Piphat">Piphat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khrueang_sai" title="Khrueang sai">Khrueang sai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahori" title="Mahori">Mahori</a> differ in significant ways, they all share a basic instrumentation and theoretical approach. Each employs small ching hand cymbals and <a href="/wiki/Krap" title="Krap">krap</a> wooden sticks to mark the primary beat reference. Thai classical music has had a wide influence on the musical traditions of neighboring countries. The traditional <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Myanmar" title="Music of Myanmar">music of Myanmar</a> was strongly influenced by the Thai music repertoire, called Yodaya (ယိုးဒယား), which was brought over from the <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya Kingdom</a>. As Siam expanded its political and cultural influence to Laos and Cambodia during the early Rattanakosin period, its music was quickly absorbed by the Cambodia and Lao courts.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Thailand" title="Cinema of Thailand">Cinema of Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thai_television_soap_opera" title="Thai television soap opera">Thai television soap opera</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:255px;max-width:255px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tony_Jaa_cropped.JPG"><img class="thumbimage"><a class="image" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/180819_%EB%B8%94%EB%9E%99%ED%95%91%ED%81%AC_%ED%8C%AC%EC%8B%B8%EC%9D%B8%ED%9A%8C_%EC%BD%94%EC%97%91%EC%8A%A4_%EB%9D%BC%EC%9D%B4%EB%B8%8C%ED%94%84%EB%9D%BC%EC%9E%90_%EB%A6%AC%EC%82%AC.jpg/176px-180819_%EB%B8%94%EB%9E%99%ED%95%91%ED%81%AC_%ED%8C%AC%EC%8B%B8%EC%9D%B8%ED%9A%8C_%EC%BD%94%EC%97%91%EC%8A%A4_%EB%9D%BC%EC%9D%B4%EB%B8%8C%ED%94%84%EB%9D%BC%EC%9E%90_%EB%A6%AC%EC%82%AC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/180819_%EB%B8%94%EB%9E%99%ED%95%91%ED%81%AC_%ED%8C%AC%EC%8B%B8%EC%9D%B8%ED%9A%8C_%EC%BD%94%EC%97%91%EC%8A%A4_%EB%9D%BC%EC%9D%B4%EB%B8%8C%ED%94%84%EB%9D%BC%EC%9E%90_%EB%A6%AC%EC%82%AC.jpg/234px-180819_%EB%B8%94%EB%9E%99%ED%95%91%ED%81%AC_%ED%8C%AC%EC%8B%B8%EC%9D%B8%ED%9A%8C_%EC%BD%94%EC%97%91%EC%8A%A4_%EB%9D%BC%EC%9D%B4%EB%B8%8C%ED%94%84%EB%9D%BC%EC%9E%90_%EB%A6%AC%EC%82%AC.jpg 2x" width="117"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phanom_Yeerum" title="Phanom Yeerum">Phanom Yeerum</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lalisa_Manoban" title="Lalisa Manoban">Lalisa Manoban</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>Thai films are exported and exhibited in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[229]</a></sup> Thai cinema has developed its own unique identity and now being internationally recognized for their culture-driven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[230]</a></sup> Films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Ong-Bak:_Muay_Thai_Warrior" title="Ong-Bak: Muay Thai Warrior">Ong-Bak: Muay Thai Warrior</a></i> (2003) and <i><a href="/wiki/Tom-Yum-Goong" title="Tom-Yum-Goong">Tom-Yum-Goong</a></i> (2005), starred <a href="/wiki/Tony_Jaa" title="Tony Jaa">Tony Jaa</a>, feature distinctive aspects of Thai martial arts "<a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a>".
</p><p>Thai horror has always had a significant cult following, unique take on tales from beyond the grave. More recently, horror films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Shutter_(2004_film)" title="Shutter (2004 film)">Shutter</a></i> (2004), was one of the best-known Thai horror movies and recognized worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[231]</a></sup> Other examples include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Unseeable" title="The Unseeable">The Unseeable</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Alone_(2007_film)" title="Alone (2007 film)">Alone</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Body_(2007_film)" title="Body (2007 film)">Body</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Coming_Soon_(2008_film)" title="Coming Soon (2008 film)">Coming Soon</a></i> (2008), <i><a href="/wiki/4bia" title="4bia">4bia</a></i> (2008), <i><a href="/wiki/Phobia_2" title="Phobia 2">Phobia 2</a></i> (2009), <i><a href="/wiki/Ladda_Land" title="Ladda Land">Ladda Land</a></i> (2011), <i><a href="/wiki/Pee_Mak" title="Pee Mak">Pee Mak</a></i> (2013), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Promise_(2017_film)" title="The Promise (2017 film)">The Promise</a></i> (2017), and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Medium_(2021_film)" title="The Medium (2021 film)">The Medium</a></i> (2021).
</p><p>Thai heist thriller film <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_Genius" title="Bad Genius">Bad Genius</a></i> (2017), was one of the most internationally successful Thai film, It broke Thai film earning records in several Asian countries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[232]</a></sup> Bad Genius won in 12 categories at the 27th <a href="/wiki/Suphannahong_National_Film_Awards" title="Suphannahong National Film Awards">Suphannahong National Film Awards</a>, and also won the Jury Award at the 16th <a href="/wiki/New_York_Asian_Film_Festival" title="New York Asian Film Festival">New York Asian Film Festival</a> with a worldwide collection of more than $42 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[233]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thailand television dramas, known as <a href="/wiki/Thai_television_soap_opera" title="Thai television soap opera">Lakorn</a>, Lakorn have become popular in Thailand and its neighbours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[234]</a></sup> Many dramas tend to have a romantic focus, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Khluen_Chiwit" title="Khluen Chiwit">Khluen Chiwit</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U-Prince" title="U-Prince">U-Prince</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ugly_Duckling_(TV_series)" title="Ugly Duckling (TV series)">Ugly Duckling</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crown_Princess" title="The Crown Princess">The Crown Princess</a></i> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teen_drama" title="Teen drama">teen dramas</a> television series, such as <i><a href="/wiki/2gether:_The_Series_(Thai_TV_series)" title="2gether: The Series (Thai TV series)">2gether: The Series</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gifted_(Thai_TV_series)" title="The Gifted (Thai TV series)">The Gifted</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Girl_From_Nowhere" title="Girl From Nowhere">Girl From Nowhere</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hormones:_The_Series" title="Hormones: The Series">Hormones: The Series</a></i>.
</p><p>The Entertainment industries (film and television) are estimated to have directly contributed $2.1 billion in gross domestic product (GDP) to the Thai economy in 2011. They also directly supported 86,600 jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[235]</a></sup> Amongst several <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">Dance-pop</a> artists who have made internationally successful can be mentioned "Lisa" <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lalisa_Manoban" title="Lalisa Manoban">Lalisa Manoban</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[236]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tata_Young" title="Tata Young">Tata Young</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Thailand" title="Cuisine of Thailand">Cuisine of Thailand</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:122px;max-width:122px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaeng_matsaman_kai.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Kaeng_matsaman_kai.JPG/120px-Kaeng_matsaman_kai.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Kaeng_matsaman_kai.JPG/180px-Kaeng_matsaman_kai.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Kaeng_matsaman_kai.JPG/240px-Kaeng_matsaman_kai.JPG 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mango_sticy_rice_(3859549574).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Mango_sticy_rice_%283859549574%29.jpg/180px-Mango_sticy_rice_%283859549574%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Mango_sticy_rice_%283859549574%29.jpg/270px-Mango_sticy_rice_%283859549574%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Mango_sticy_rice_%283859549574%29.jpg/360px-Mango_sticy_rice_%283859549574%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Massaman_curry" title="Massaman curry">chicken massaman curry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mango_sticky_rice" title="Mango sticky rice">mango sticky rice</a></div></div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Thailand" title="Cuisine of Thailand">Thai cuisine</a> is one of the most popular in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[238]</a></sup> Thai food blends five fundamental tastes: sweet, spicy, sour, bitter, and salty. The herbs and spices most used in Thai cooking themselves have medicinal qualities such as <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lemongrass" title="Lemongrass">lemongrass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaffir_lime" title="Kaffir lime">kaffir lime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galangal" title="Galangal">galangal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turmeric" title="Turmeric">turmeric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coriander" title="Coriander">coriander</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[239]</a></sup> Each region of Thailand has its specialities: <i>kaeng khiao wan</i> (<a href="/wiki/Green_curry" title="Green curry">green curry</a>) in the central region, <i>som tam</i> (<a href="/wiki/Green_papaya_salad" title="Green papaya salad">green papaya salad</a>) in the northeast, <i><a href="/wiki/Khao_soi" title="Khao soi">khao soi</a></i> in the north, and <a href="/wiki/Massaman_curry" title="Massaman curry"><i>massaman</i> curry</a> in the south.
</p><p>In 2017, seven Thai dishes appeared on a list of the "World's 50 Best Foods"— an online worldwide poll by <i><a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> Travel</i>. Thailand had more dishes on the list than any other country. They were: <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tom_yam" title="Tom yam">tom yam</a> goong</i> (4th), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pad_Thai" title="Pad Thai">pad Thai</a></i> (5th), <i>som tam</i> (6th), <i>massaman</i> curry (10th), <a href="/wiki/Green_curry" title="Green curry">green curry</a> (19th), <a href="/wiki/Thai_fried_rice" title="Thai fried rice">Thai fried rice</a> (24th) and <i><a href="/wiki/Nam_tok_mu" title="Nam tok mu">mu nam tok</a></i> (36th).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN-2017_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-2017-251">[240]</a></sup> Two desserts were also listed in CNN’s 50 Best Desserts Around The World: <a href="/wiki/Mango_sticky_rice" title="Mango sticky rice">mango sticky rice</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tub_tim_krob" title="Tub tim krob">tub tim krob</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[241]</a></sup>
</p><p>The staple food in Thailand is rice, particularly <a href="/wiki/Jasmine_rice" title="Jasmine rice">jasmine rice</a> (also known as <i>hom Mali</i>) which forms part of almost every meal. Thailand is a leading exporter of rice, and Thais consume over 100 kg of milled rice per person per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRRI-WRS_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRRI-WRS-253">[242]</a></sup> Thailand is also the world leader in edible insect industry<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[243]</a></sup> and well-known for its street food; Bangkok is sometimes called the street food capital of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[245]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Units_of_measurement">Units of measurement</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Thai_units_of_measurement" title="Thai units of measurement">Thai units of measurement</a></div>
<p>Thailand generally uses the <a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric system</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Thai_units_of_measurement" title="Thai units of measurement">traditional units of measurement</a> for land area are used, and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_units" title="Imperial units">imperial units</a> of measurement are occasionally used for building materials, such as wood and plumbing fixtures. Years are numbered as B.E. (<a href="/wiki/Thai_solar_calendar" title="Thai solar calendar">Buddhist Era</a>) in educational settings, civil service, government, contracts, and newspaper datelines. However, in banking, and increasingly in industry and commerce, standard Western year (Christian or Common Era) counting is the standard practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[246]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Thailand_at_the_Olympics" title="Thailand at the Olympics">Thailand at the Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Thailand" title="Rugby union in Thailand">Rugby union in Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf_in_Thailand" title="Golf in Thailand">Golf in Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Thailand" title="Football in Thailand">Football in Thailand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_sporting_events_held_in_Thailand" title="List of sporting events held in Thailand">List of sporting events held in Thailand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Muay_Thai_Fight_Us_Vs_Burma_(80668065).jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1366" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Muay_Thai_Fight_Us_Vs_Burma_%2880668065%29.jpeg/200px-Muay_Thai_Fight_Us_Vs_Burma_%2880668065%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Muay_Thai_Fight_Us_Vs_Burma_%2880668065%29.jpeg/300px-Muay_Thai_Fight_Us_Vs_Burma_%2880668065%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Muay_Thai_Fight_Us_Vs_Burma_%2880668065%29.jpeg/400px-Muay_Thai_Fight_Us_Vs_Burma_%2880668065%29.jpeg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Muay_Thai_Fight_Us_Vs_Burma_(80668065).jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a>, Thailand's signature sport</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">มวยไทย</span>, RTGS: Muai Thai, <small></small><span class="IPA" lang="th-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Thai" title="Help:IPA/Thai">[muaj tʰaj]</a></span>, lit. "Thai boxing") is a <a href="/wiki/Combat_sport" title="Combat sport">combat sport</a> of Thailand that uses stand-up striking along with various <a href="/wiki/Clinch_fighting" title="Clinch fighting">clinching</a> techniques. Muay Thai became widespread internationally in the late-20th to 21st century, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westernized" title="Westernized">Westernized</a> practitioners from Thailand began competing in <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">kickboxing</a> and mixed rules matches as well as matches under muay Thai rules around the world, Famous practitioners such as <a href="/wiki/Buakaw_Banchamek" title="Buakaw Banchamek">Buakaw Banchamek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samart_Payakaroon" title="Samart Payakaroon">Samart Payakaroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dieselnoi_Chor_Thanasukarn" title="Dieselnoi Chor Thanasukarn">Dieselnoi Chor Thanasukarn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apidej_Sit-Hirun" title="Apidej Sit-Hirun">Apidej Sit-Hirun</a>. <a href="/wiki/Buakaw_Banchamek" title="Buakaw Banchamek">Buakaw Banchamek</a> has probably brought more international interest in Muay Thai than any other Muay Thai fighters ever had.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muaythaicitizen_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-muaythaicitizen-258">[247]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> has overtaken muay Thai as the most widely followed sport in contemporary Thai society. <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_football_team" title="Thailand national football team">Thailand national football team</a> has played the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a> six times and reached the semifinals in 1972. The country has hosted the Asian Cup twice, in 1972 and in 2007. The 2007 edition was co-hosted together with <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. It is not uncommon to see Thais cheering their favourite English Premier League teams on television and walking around in replica kit. Another widely enjoyed pastime, and once a competitive sport, is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kite_flying" title="Kite flying">kite flying</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">Volleyball</a> is rapidly growing as one of the most popular sports. The <a href="/wiki/Thailand_women%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Thailand women's national volleyball team">women's team</a> has often participated in the <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Women's World Championship">World Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="FIVB Volleyball Women's World Cup">World Cup</a>, and <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_World_Grand_Prix" title="FIVB Volleyball World Grand Prix">World Grand Prix</a> <a href="/wiki/Asian_Championship" title="Asian Championship">Asian Championship</a>. They have won the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Women%27s_Volleyball_Championship" title="Asian Women's Volleyball Championship">Asian Championship</a> twice and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AVC_Cup_for_Women" title="AVC Cup for Women">Asian Cup</a> once. By the success of the women's team, the <a href="/wiki/Thailand_men%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Thailand men's national volleyball team">men team</a> has been growing as well.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Takraw" title="Takraw">Takraw</a> (Thai: ตะกร้อ) is a sport native to Thailand, in which the players hit a rattan ball and are only allowed to use their feet, knees, chest, and head to touch the ball. <a href="/wiki/Sepak_takraw" title="Sepak takraw">Sepak takraw</a> is a form of this sport which is similar to volleyball. The players must volley a ball over a net and force it to hit the ground on the opponent's side. It is also a popular sport in other countries in Southeast Asia. A rather similar game but played only with the feet is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buka_ball" title="Buka ball">buka ball</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">Snooker</a> has enjoyed increasing popularity in Thailand in recent years, with interest in the game being stimulated by the success of Thai snooker player <a href="/wiki/James_Wattana" title="James Wattana">James Wattana</a> in the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[248]</a></sup> Other notable players produced by the country include <a href="/wiki/Ratchayothin_Yotharuck" title="Ratchayothin Yotharuck">Ratchayothin Yotharuck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noppon_Saengkham" title="Noppon Saengkham">Noppon Saengkham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dechawat_Poomjaeng" title="Dechawat Poomjaeng">Dechawat Poomjaeng</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[249]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rugby is also a growing sport in Thailand with the <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_rugby_union_team" title="Thailand national rugby union team">Thailand national rugby union team</a> rising to be ranked 61st in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[250]</a></sup> Thailand became the first country in the world to host an international 80 welterweight rugby tournament in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[251]</a></sup> The national domestic Thailand Rugby Union (TRU) competition includes several universities and services teams such as <a href="/wiki/Chulalongkorn_University" title="Chulalongkorn University">Chulalongkorn University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahasarakham_University" title="Mahasarakham University">Mahasarakham University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kasetsart_University" title="Kasetsart University">Kasetsart University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Songkla_University" title="Prince of Songkla University">Prince of Songkla University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thammasat_University" title="Thammasat University">Thammasat University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rangsit_University" title="Rangsit University">Rangsit University</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Police" title="Thai Police">Thai Police</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Army" title="Thai Army">Thai Army</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Navy" title="Thai Navy">Thai Navy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Air_Force" title="Royal Thai Air Force">Royal Thai Air Force</a>. Local sports clubs which also compete in the TRU include the British Club of Bangkok, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southerners_Sports_Club_(Bangkok)" title="Southerners Sports Club (Bangkok)">Southerners Sports Club (Bangkok)</a> and the Royal Bangkok Sports Club.
</p><p>Thailand has been called the golf capital of Asia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[252]</a></sup> as it is a popular destination for golf. The country attracts a large number of golfers from Japan, Korea, Singapore, South Africa, and Western countries who come to play golf in Thailand every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[253]</a></sup> The growing popularity of golf, especially among the middle classes and immigrants, is evident as there are more than 200 world-class golf courses nationwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[254]</a></sup> and some of them are chosen to host PGA and LPGA tournaments, such as <a href="/wiki/Amata_Spring_Country_Club" title="Amata Spring Country Club">Amata Spring Country Club</a>, Alpine Golf and Sports Club, Thai Country Club, and Black Mountain Golf Club.
</p><p>Basketball is a growing sport in Thailand, especially on the professional sports club level. The Chang Thailand Slammers won the 2011 <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Basketball_League" title="ASEAN Basketball League">ASEAN Basketball League</a> Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[255]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thailand_national_basketball_team" title="Thailand national basketball team">Thailand national basketball team</a> had its most successful year at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_1966_Asian_Games" title="Basketball at the 1966 Asian Games">1966 Asian Games</a> where it won the silver medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[256]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other sports in Thailand are slowly growing as the country develops its sporting infrastructure. The success in sports like <a href="/wiki/Powerlifting" title="Powerlifting">weightlifting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a> at the last two summer Olympic Games has demonstrated that boxing is no longer the only medal option for Thailand.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bangkok_Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="902" data-file-width="1498" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bangkok_Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium_1.jpg/220px-Bangkok_Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bangkok_Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium_1.jpg/330px-Bangkok_Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bangkok_Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium_1.jpg/440px-Bangkok_Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bangkok_Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium" title="Lumpinee Boxing Stadium">Lumpinee Boxing Stadium</a></div></div></div>
<p>The well-known <a href="/wiki/Lumpinee_Boxing_Stadium" title="Lumpinee Boxing Stadium">Lumpinee Boxing Stadium</a> originally sited at Rama IV Road near Lumphini Park hosted its final Muay Thai boxing matches on 8 February 2014 after the venue first opened in December 1956. Managed by the Royal Thai Army, the stadium was officially selected for the purpose of muay Thai bouts following a competition that was staged on 15 March 1956. From 11 February 2014, the stadium will relocate to Ram Intra Road, due to the new venue's capacity to accommodate audiences of up to 3,500. Foreigners typically pay between 1,000 and 2,000 baht to view a match, with prices depending on the location of the seating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[257]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thammasat Stadium is a multi-purpose stadium in Bangkok. It is currently used mostly for football matches. The stadium holds 25,000. It is on Thammasat University's Rangsit campus. It was built for the <a href="/wiki/1998_Asian_Games" title="1998 Asian Games">1998 Asian Games</a> by construction firm Christiani and Nielsen, the same company that constructed the Democracy Monument in Bangkok.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajamangala_National_Stadium" title="Rajamangala National Stadium">Rajamangala National Stadium</a> is the biggest sporting arena in Thailand. It currently has a capacity of 65,000. It is in Bang Kapi, Bangkok. The stadium was built in 1998 for the 1998 Asian Games and is the home stadium of the <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_football_team" title="Thailand national football team">Thailand national football team</a>.
</p>

See Gerini, Ptolemy, p. 170. But Samarade is near Bangkok and there can hardly have been Thais there in Ptolemy's time, and Footnote 190: So too in Central Asia Kustana appears to be a learned distortion of the name <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khotan" title="Khotan">Khotan</a>, made to give it a meaning in Sanskrit.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Project+Gutenberg+EBook+of+Hinduism+and+Buddhism%2C+An+Historical+Sketch%2C+Vol.+3+%28of+3%29+%5BEBook+%2316847%5D&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pages=Ch.+xxxvii+1%2C+citing+in+turn+Footnote+189%3A+The+name+is+found+on+Champan+inscriptions+of+1050+CE+and+according+to+Gerini+appears+in+Ptolemy%27s+Geographia%7CSamarade+%3D+S%C3%A2mara%E1%B9%AD%E1%B9%ADha.+See+Gerini%2C+Ptolemy%2C+p.+170.+But+Samarade+is+near+Bangkok+and+there+can+hardly+have+been+Thais+there+in+Ptolemy%27s+time%2C+and+Footnote+190%3A+So+too+in+Central+Asia+Kustana+appears+to+be+a+learned+distortion+of+the+name+Khotan%2C+made+to+give+it+a+meaning+in+Sanskrit&amp;rft.pub=Routledge+%26+Kegan+Paul+Ltd.&amp;rft.date=1921&amp;rft.aulast=Eliot&amp;rft.aufirst=Charles&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThailand"></span></span>
